<ul><li>QCT (Qualcomm CDMA Technologies): CDMA wireless products; 60 percent of revenue</li>
<li>QTL (Qualcomm Technology Licensing): Licensing; 19% of revenue</li>
<li>QSI (Qualcomm strategic initiatives): Investing in other tech companies; 1% of revenue</li></ul><p>Qualcomm is a predominantly fabless provider of semiconductor products for wireless communications and data transfer in portable devices.<sup id="cite_ref-newceo_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newceo-222">[222]</a></sup> According to the analyst firm Strategy Analytics, Qualcomm has a 39 percent market-share for smartphone application processors and a 50 percent market-share of baseband processors.<sup id="cite_ref-FierceWireless_2016_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FierceWireless_2016-223">[223]</a></sup> Its share of the market for application processors on tablets is 18 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup> According to analyst firm ABI Research, Qualcomm has a 65 percent market-share in LTE baseband.<sup id="cite_ref-Mott_2017_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mott_2017-225">[225]</a></sup> Qualcomm also provides licenses to use its patents, many of which are critical to the CDMA2000, TD-SCDMA and WCDMA wireless standards.<sup id="cite_ref-Asif2011_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Asif2011-226">[226]</a></sup> The company is estimated to earn $20 for every smartphone sold.<sup id="cite_ref-Cannady2013_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cannady2013-227">[227]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>64</span></sup></p><p>Qualcomm is the largest public company in San Diego.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-six_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-six-7">[7]</a></sup> It has a philanthropic arm called The Qualcomm Foundation.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup> A January 2013 lawsuit resulted in Qualcomm voluntarily adopting a policy of disclosing its political contributions. According to <i>The New York Times</i>, Qualcomm's new disclosure policy was praised by transparency advocates.<sup id="cite_ref-randomname_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-randomname-231">[231]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(6)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Qualcomm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: See also" data-section="24" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-6 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-6">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Qualcomm_Snapdragon" title="Qualcomm Snapdragon">Qualcomm Snapdragon</a></li></ul></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(7)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Qualcomm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: References" data-section="25" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-7 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-7">

<li id="cite_note-six-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-six_7-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-six_7-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite id="CITEREFWest" class="citation">West, Joel, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.sandiegohistory.org/journal/v55-1/pdf/v55-1west.pdf"><i>Before Qualcomm: Linkabit and the Origins of San Diego’s Telecom Industry</i></a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>, The Journal of San Diego History<span class="reference-accessdate">, retrieved <span class="nowrap">August 9,</span> 2014</span></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Before+Qualcomm%3A+Linkabit+and+the+Origins+of+San+Diego%E2%80%99s+Telecom+Industry&amp;rft.pub=The+Journal+of+San+Diego+History&amp;rft.aulast=West&amp;rft.aufirst=Joel&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.sandiegohistory.org%2Fjournal%2Fv55-1%2Fpdf%2Fv55-1west.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AQualcomm" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r935243608"></span>
